Chapter XXV.
About the veins in the extremities of the nose.
Most bruises occur in the extremities of the nose, and they are treated and bandaged within a few days during which one must take care of it.
And for this reason, you should treat it at the beginning of its appearance, and continue treating it entirely. And then pause on the place where you cauterized or applied a burning medicine, which was in that location.
But if treatment is delayed until it has become inflamed, hard, dark in color, and insensitive, then do not touch it with an iron instrument as it may be a chronic abscess; for many times the person treating this abscess improperly causes great harm to the patient.
And if the abscess is soft to touch and not dark in color, and if treatment is possible at all times, then evacuate the pus without fear, and treat the area with something that dries and constricts until it heals.
Chapter XXVI.
On suturing the nose and lips and the ear when continuity is lost due to plague or similar causes.
Know that when the continuity is lost in one of these cartilages, few would undertake such an operation except in some cases.
Therefore, when dealing with any of these causes, you must consider whether it is a fresh wound or due to the natural course of healing, and then you should approximate the two edges of the wound with stitches, and afterwards treat it until it heals.
And if the lips of a wound of continuity are already separated, and each one is made healthy, now you must excise each part of its visible edge until it bleeds. And then adjust the two lips with sutures and strengthen them, and sprinkle over them powder of dragon's blood and thrisse, and place upon the powder a piece of mastic plaster or some other consolidating plaster, and leave that wound for two days or three, and then untie it and change the plaster and leave it until the pus has ceased to flow, and then treat with an ointment until it is healed.
The method of the suture is that you join the wound of continuity either with needles as we have recommended for the suture of the abdomen, or join the wound of continuity with thread as you know how to do.
Chapter XXVII.
Of the extraction of those causes that appear in the two lips in their inner parts.
Many times in some men in the inner parts of their lips there appear abscesses that are hard like the gristle of birds, and some of them are smaller and some are larger.
Therefore, you should turn the lips and split each of those hardnesses from all sides, and then when you excise them, fill the place with thrisse-dressed cloth until the blood is constricted, and then wash it with vinegar water and treat the area with astringents until it is healed.
Chapter XXVIII.
Of the incision of flesh adjusted to the gums.
Great care must be taken when dealing with flesh attached to the gum. The ancients called this condition albulus. Then you should suspend the affected area for about an ounce or hold it between your forceps and incise along its root, allowing the pus to drain or the blood to flow.
And afterwards apply powder that is soothing or other styptic powders or excitants to the area.
And if the flesh returns, then incise it again, and cauterize it, for after cauterization it will not return.
Chapter XXIX.
Of the extraction of teeth with iron.
When on the surface of the teeth in the inner parts and those from outside, and between the gums to which they are attached, there are rough spots, ulcers, and some areas are blackened and appear yellowish or greenish, causing corruption to the gum and making the teeth decayed.
And therefore you should make the patient sit between your hands and place his head in a warm towel, and extract the teeth on which these rough spots appear along with any grit inside them so that none of it remains, and this will remove the blackness and yellowish color and other issues until they are cleansed.
If this can be done at the beginning of the extraction, it is good; but if not, then you should repeat the extraction on those teeth another day and on the second and third days until it reaches the final step as you desire.
And know that teeth have need of various instruments of different forms and shapes according to what is prepared for your operation. And therefore, the razors which are used to remove the tooth that is to be extracted are different from those used to rasp between the teeth according to other forms, and these forms of razors you should prepare as you will see shortly:
Chapter XXX.
On the Extraction of Teeth.
When you wish to cure the tooth of its pain by completely extracting it and delaying in the total extraction of it, know that there is no reason to postpone the removal when it needs to be extracted, since it is a substance that requires promptness in its extraction.
But when the patient is forced to have that tooth extracted, you must be firmly certain which is the painful tooth, because often the pain can deceive the patient and lead them to believe it is in a healthy tooth. If you extract the wrong one, the pain will not cease until the diseased and painful tooth is removed, as we have already seen through the experience of many operations.
Therefore, when you need to be certain which is the painful tooth, and once you know well, it is necessary that you scarify around the tooth with an instrument that has some virtue until it dissolves the tooth from the gum completely. Then, using your fingers or fine forceps, begin gently at first, little by little, until you can loosen it.
And then use strong forceps for good leverage or a firm hold, and place the patient's head between your hands in such a way that they feel comfortable and secure. Then pull the tooth straight so as not to break it, nor cause greater pain to the patient.
And thus if it is not dislocated, now take one of those instruments and place it there from all sides with ease and strive for the removal of it as was done at the beginning.
But if the tooth is loose or decayed, now cover it with cloth that you have prepared and bind it tightly at the end with a thin thread so that it does not become dislodged during your compression upon that tooth holding it.
And it is necessary that you work extremely carefully around the incision in a circle all around the gum and be mindful of your strength so as not to tear that which should remain intact, and return to the diseased area for the malice that it may be better than the initial pain.
And be careful that you do not do what some ignorant barbers do in their foolishness and audacity during the removal of teeth; for they often fail to administer what we have recommended. Many times this brings upon sick people great evils which are much harder to cure, and the roots of those teeth become badly damaged, or some of them, or you may extract it along with some bones of the jaw as many times we have witnessed.
And after the removal of it, the mouth should be washed with warm water or salt water.
And if there is bleeding for this reason, as often happens, now take some quantity of wax and sprinkle it over the wound, and if that does not stop the bleeding, use cauterization.
The shape of the forceps and the delicate handles with which the tooth is held at the beginning should be of long extremity, short handle, and thick, so that they do not bend when you are working with them.
And so they should be as if made of thick material so that when stranguries are applied to them, they not be folded but rather have short extremities.
And they should be made of Indian iron, straight in their extremities. And at the extremities of those there are teeth among which some enter into others and constrict with great force, and sometimes the extremities of those should have the shape of a bird's beak called ciconia, that is a heron, and they are very strong in constriction.
Chapter XXXI.
On the extraction of teeth and the removal of bones from locked jaws.
When you must perform the extraction of a tooth that is locked due to some cause, it is necessary for you to apply poultices around the area for one day or two until the area becomes softened. The shape of the second instrument is that it be triangular and have a very fine tip.

And another skill is to know the instruments for the teeth and to make them similar to other instruments.
But the skilled and subtle artisan finds for himself according to what he understands about the operation and various diseases; because there are diseases about which the ancients did not say or make a proper instrument, due to the forms of different kinds.

Chapter xxxii.
On the treatment of prominent teeth over other teeth.
When the prominent teeth do not follow their natural course and the form is lax, especially when this affects women, and more so those who are venerable; then you should consider: if a tooth is too close to another tooth, and it is impossible to extract or apply medication, at that time remove its root. But ensure that it is not attached to another tooth; then you cut it with this instrument which has the following form; it resembles a pig's snout, and it is made of Indian steel with an extremely sharp point.
And ensure your incision with which you cut it is not made too deep due to the hardness of the tooth, and that it does not communicate with other teeth.
And if it is a prominent tooth that can be filed down, then file it with an Indian steel file which has the following form:
And it should be entirely made of Indian steel and should be sharp; it should have very fine points as with a file used to make needles, with which the tooth is filed little by little over several days with ease, so that it does not communicate with another tooth and cause damage. And smooth it at the end, and polish it with some razors.
And if it is a tooth where part of it is broken and you run your tongue over it, then you should file down the inside until the roughness of that fracture is smoothed and filled so that your tongue does not get hurt and the speech is not impaired.
Chapter XXXIII.
On the restoration of bad teeth with gold or silver filling.
When it happens that the front teeth are loose or dislocated due to impact or accident, and the patient cannot bear what they eat because of this, and you have treated them with astringent medicines but your treatment has not been effective, then for those that do not heal, you should proceed by restoring them with gold filling and not silver, because silver changes color and may cause issues after some days, whereas gold never changes.
And the filling should be in such subtlety and fineness according to the quantity that can fit between the teeth; the method of restoration is that you take the filling and place twice its amount between two healthy teeth, and then shape it with two tortuosities of the filling between one or multiple bad teeth, so that it reaches the healthy tooth on the other side. And then continue the restoration from the part where you began, and strengthen your work with ease and wisdom so that it is not defective.
And when you are restoring the filling, be careful not to expose the roots of the teeth.
And then trim the excess filling with forceps or scissors, and place it in each location by hand, and shape it to conceal it between the healthy tooth and the bad tooth so that it does not injure the tongue. And then shape it as finely as a ribbon.
But if it becomes loose or broken, reinforce that part with additional filling in such a way throughout its duration.
And this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the alignment of two healthy teeth and of two misaligned teeth, as you will see these diagrams:
And when it happens that I return one tooth or two near the placement of each in their places, and they grow back as we have recounted, and they become aligned.
And only a good artisan and wise person can do this.
And sometimes a similar piece of cowbone is used for some reason in the shape of a tooth, and it is placed in the location where the tooth is missing, and it is fixed as we have said, and remains and serves there for a long time.
Chapter XXXIV.
On the incision of the membrane that is in the tongue and prevents speech.
This membrane that is under the tongue sometimes is natural and one is born with it, or it is accidental and occurs due to an injury that has already healed.
And the operation is that one opens the mouth of the patient, and lifts their tongue; then one cuts that membrane along the nerve according to its length, ensuring the tongue is sufficiently exposed.
But if there is any hardness or knot in that area, and this is due to the healing of an injury, then you should cut carefully and divide it along its length until the knot dissolves.
And be careful not to make a cut in the surface of the flesh so that you do not sever the arteries and cause bleeding.
After washing the remnants of the incision with water or vinegar or clean water, put a piece of linen under the tongue; this is done so that the bad taste does not remain under the tongue each night so that it does not become consolidated elsewhere.
If bleeding occurs, place over the area vitriol powder; but if the blood flows continuously, then cauterize the area with a hot iron, which is appropriate for this condition. And subsequently treat it with other causes until it is healed.
Chapter XXXV.
On the extraction of a ranula under the tongue.
Sometimes, an abscess appears under the tongue, resembling a small swelling that prevents the tongue from performing its normal function; and it grows so much that it fills the mouth.
The operation to be performed is to open the mouth wide in front of the light and examine the abscess.
And if you see it as dark or black in color, hard, and without any sensation, then do not touch what appears to be gangrenous.
And if it is inclined towards whiteness and moisture, then you should proceed with the operation, incising it with a fine scalpel, and cut it entirely; and if blood flows during your procedure, then place over it powdered zinc sulfate, which is vitriol, to stop the bleeding.
And then return to your work once you have completed the procedure, washing it with vinegar and salt; and treat it with other appropriate treatments until it is healed.
Chapter xxxvi.
On the extraction of abscesses from both armpits and those that occur in the groin and other abscesses.
When you find an abscess in the groin area, these are glands that are assembled there, which appear outside and are called armpits. When you treat them as we have said in the division and they do not heal, then consider if the abscess is hard, dark in color, and has little sensation; at this point, do not touch it with iron.
And if it is red in color and the root is large, then do not touch it with iron due to the flow of blood. Instead, leave it inside to mature, and either you will remove it later, or it may rupture on its own.
And if it is white in color, soft, and the root is delicate, then that should be incised.
And the operation on it is that you consider, before your operation, whether the abscess has already begun to mature after being cauterized or if it has decreased in some way. Then have the patient sit facing the sunlight, and his head towards your side, and expose the opening of the abscess, and the assistant holding firmly with their hands the instrument mentioned below:
And it should be made of silver or iron, and should be as thin as a knife.
When you press with that instrument and the abscess is revealed to you, place your finger over it firmly, then take some of it and insert it into the opening, and pull it outwards as much as you can. Here is another illustration of cutting through one cause of the tunics, and appropriately proceed with this instrument which has this form:
Here is another illustration of cutting through one cause of the tunics, and appropriately proceed with this instrument which has this form: and it is similar to forceps, but the extremities of its are curved, thus the opening of each of those is in line with the other, sharp points, which are made of iron.
If this instrument is not available to you, then proceed with this spatula which has the following form: It is sharp on one side, not sharp on the other side.
And after you have made one incision, make the other following this method of cutting, and then wash the wound with clean water for healing.
But if there is bleeding, treat it with water from the decoction of lemon peel or mint leaves and similar astringents until the flow of blood is stopped, and then proceed to heal it once it is stabilized.
And sometimes there arise in the throat other abscesses or those affecting both ears, and cut these according to what I have said about cutting two incisions equally.
And I had treated a woman with an abscess that was born in her throat, which abscess tended to have a dark color and little sensation, and it had already closed the throat of hers, and she breathed only through a narrow passage, and I had already prohibited her from eating and drinking water, and she would have reached death if not for treatment within one day or two.
And the abscess had already grown so much that it had formed two paths through which it could drain by two tracts.
Then I cut it surgically and placed it in one of their pieces, and pulled that, and from there the larger portion was detached, and then I incised that so as to understand the other part, and then I closed its mouth, and compressed its tongue, and then I placed the piece in that abscess.
And then I removed a large part of it, and only a little blood came from it. Then the fever of that woman subsided, and she began to drink water immediately, and soon after she ate food. Therefore, I did not cease to incise that abscess for several long periods, and an abscess succeeded in its place, which I incised until it was prolonged.
Then I applied something and cauterized the fever of it, then there was an addition to it; and afterward I wandered about and did not know what God would do next with that.
Chapter XXXVII.
On the incision of the breast when it is abscessed.
When one observes catarr in the breast, and it is abscessed and elongated, then it is called perpendicular; and if it is in the lower part thick and round, then it is called a buba.
But when it is cured as we have said in the division and you do not confirm your treatment, and similarly often times an abscess cauterized remains stubborn and subtle, then it is necessary that you incise the one that is aggregated roundly; and if it reaches a certain length and is bloody, of dark color or black, and is not in the center, then it is necessary that you attempt its incision, because there is fear of malady in that.
And when you see it according to the method that I have said about its whiteness and length, that you make the patient sit and press the tongue with an instrument of which the form is appropriate, and place the incision in the new area, and pull it down and cut it with one of two instruments which are mentioned in the cutting of two membranes.
And you should not cut it unless it is adjusted to the natural limit without excess, for if you cut too much, you will impair their speech.
And after the incision, use what we have recommended for the incision of two membranes, and treat it until it is healed.
But if the patient is frightened by the incision, you should use something to cauterize it without causing fear, and the method of cauterization is nothing but with sharp water. Place the head of the patient in your lap, then press the tongue with the instrument we have mentioned, and afterward take the water which we have described in the chapter on cauterization, and apply it there as a hot cautery, and place it neither thick nor thin, and with that fill the concavity of the instrument whose form is as follows:
Let the extremity of the cautery on which the medicine is placed be like the concavity of a spoon, and place the instrument with the medicine over the ulcer, and let the patient lie on their side so that saliva or mucus from the mouth does not flow out from it for any reason onto the wound and thus injure it.
And then take the instrument with the medicine and apply it to the uvula for about half an hour until you see it become blackened and numbed by the bite of the medicine.
And if you want, take a piece of cloth and wrap it around the end of the vein, then dip the cloth in the medicine, and insert the vein along with the cloth into a cannula so that the cloth adheres to that cannula, and do this as many times as necessary until you achieve what you want from cauterizing the grape, and afterwards let it dry until it falls off after three or four days.
And if you need to repeat the medicine, do so, and after that cauterize around the grape with a cloth soaked in the medicine, and modify what is around it according to what is prescribed by the medicine, and let it be washed with soap water, and treat it externally with an embrocation, and attend to it internally with medications until it is healed.
And this method of treatment is safer than incision and more enduring without fear.
In some cases, the grape is cured with something that cauterizes more gently than incision, for it is treated with sublimation in this manner: take plasters, hyssop, mint, rue, Arabian saffron, chamomile, and similar herbs, and mix all these ingredients or some of them in a vessel, and let them be immersed in sour grape juice and boiled; then the vessel should be heated moderately over low heat, and at one end of the vessel place a tube made of straw in this manner; it can be made of silver or straw.
And insert the end into the mouth of the patient so that the vapor reaches the uvula through the tube, until the uvula is sufficiently treated.
Regarding those superficial swellings that are dry, be careful not to perform this treatment at the beginning of the onset of abscesses, for it would be too early for the abscess, and you should not do this, but rather wait for the formation of pus.
If this instrument is not available to you, now take a reed and attach to it a cover made of cloth, so that the mouth of the wound is covered, for the covering of cloth prevents the vapor from entering the mouth.
And this treatment is good for health.
Chapter XXXVIII.
On the extraction of spines and what adheres to the wound, and of other causes.
Superficial swellings that adhere to the wound or spine or any other cause.
Then you should remove what is apparent from those elements, upon which your eye rests, and press the tongue with an instrument in sunlight, so that it becomes clear to you what is in the wound.
And what does not appear and is hidden in the wound, you should make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach, for the cause attached to the wound will be easily expelled by vomiting; or have the patient swallow a piece of bread or lettuce seed or a mouthful of dry bread; or take a piece of dried sea sponge and bind it tightly with thread, and then have the patient swallow that, as when it reaches the place where spines are lodged, they will be easily expelled. Take a eel and boil it in vinegar, and let the inside be removed and the poultice be extracted; or take a rod and apply the poultice to it and with the rod treat [the patient].
If you do not forget the causes which we have mentioned, now use an instrument of lead in this form:
And let it be as thick as a small reed, and at the end of it let there be a hook which you insert into its throat with ease.
And as you proceed, keep his head raised up, and be careful not to touch the bones of his throat, so that it does not harm him or cause injury to the bone or spine, or that it harms the patient in any way.
However, the patient should gently insert it, due to his knowledge of the location of the cause and its nature, and pull his hand with the instrument up, all this according to the quantity that has been prepared within him until it is forgotten.
Chapter XXXIX.
On the extraction of a leech attached to the throat.
When the leech is treated with what we have said in the division of treatment with medicines and compresses, consider now the patient's throat in the sunlight, since you have protruded his tongue with the instrument which we recommended to you.
Then if you see the leech, gently remove it carefully with your fingertips or with small forceps.
And if it is not possible for you to remove it, now take a concave tube and insert it into the patient's throat, then place a heated iron on the concavity of the tube, and do this several times (until the leech is dead and falls off), and keep the patient from water for the entire day.
Take a clean cloth soaked in water and wipe the mouth with it; then wash the mouth with that water. Do not let any of that water be wasted for any reason; change the water every hour with its like, because as soon as the leech feels the water, it will attach itself.
If it is not possible to perform what we have recommended with this, then fumigate the area with cimetz or asafetida using the instrument we described for fumigating the uvula.
Do this, and it will fall on its own.
And here is another method of fumigation during this procedure: take an owl in which there are burning coals and cover it with a cloth that has a hole in the middle; attach one end of the instrument to this hole. Then perform the fumigation from above, and have the patient place their mouth at the end of the tube so that no smoke escapes before you know that the fumigation has reached the leeches, for they will fall as soon as they encounter it.
And if it does not work, then repeat the fumigation several times, and prevent the patient from drinking water, and give them salty and dry foods to eat, and they should not drink water. It is necessary that this regimen be strictly followed.
And this is the form of the instrument used to remove bloodsucking leeches from the throat when they are seen; it resembles forceps as well, but with some curvature. which is placed in the throat, and its end resembles the beak of a heron, which is sharpened with a file, so that when it holds something, it does not let go.
Chapter XL.
In this chapter is the summary of the speech on the preparation for the incision and division of abscesses.
Abscesses are of various types and methods, as will be recalled for each one in this book.
And they differ in the puncturing and division of them by two methods, one of which is based on the nature of the abscess itself; and by what it contains of humidity.
And the second method is according to the locations in which they occur in the body, for an abscess that occurs in the head is different from one that occurs in the buttocks; and an abscess that appears in fleshy areas is different from one that occurs at joints; and each has its treatment by operation.
And there are some abscesses that should not be punctured but left until the pus has matured or they have reached completion.
There are other abscesses that should be evacuated when they are crosswise and have not matured according to their completion, such as those near joints, because when an abscess is close to a joint, its nature prolongs itself until you can drain what is around it, and if the tendons or nerves of that joint are corrupted, it becomes a cause for contraction of that limb; or if it is near a principal member, and if you delay puncturing it before it has matured, it may affect the principal member negatively; or if it is close to the buttocks, then puncture it while it is not yet fully matured; but do not pierce it when it is raw from incomplete digestion, except for one that is near the buttocks, so that you do not leave behind a prepuce that extends into the depths of the buttocks and causes a fistula, or create an opening that does not heal. May it be known that you know the time for piercing the abscess, and this is when it is ripe.
And you know that it is ripe when there is relief from the pain and cessation of the fever, and soon after a decrease in inflammation and pulse, and sharpness at the head of the abscess, and other signs.
And you should know that the piercing should be done at the place where the pus is deepest in the abscess and coming from the highest part of its elevation.
And the piercing should always be done along the length of the flesh or body if the abscesses are in parts such as the limbs and joints, and in places near tendons, ligaments, nerves, arteries; and finally, in all locations equally where there is no reflection; for in those that do reflect, use piercing according to that member.
But when the abscess is in a fleshy location, it is best to delay the piercing until the digestion of the second stage is confirmed, as we have said; for if you pierce before this, it prolongs the illness of the patient and increases foulness, and hardens the lips of the wound and its depth.
But some abscesses should be pierced across the width of the flesh or body due to necessity, or according to what the member requires.
And you should administer a small piercing, and in large abscesses, a larger piercing or multiple sections according to the diversity of the size of the abscesses.
And other abscesses in which the treatment should be incised and opened, when it is done as said before and is performed at a time when it can already heal, such as those that occur with excessive boils and buboes.
And of those which are incised with a three-angled section; and of those in which it is incised as the figure of a myrtle leaf, such as the abscesses of the angles.
And of those in which a round section and a lunar section are administered, and similar to those.
But in the case where there is none of the above, such as superficial lion abscesses, you should puncture it with a superficial incision or simply open it up.
And when the abscess is large and has collected pus, you should puncture it but do not hesitate to extract all the pus at that moment; after extracting a portion from it, on another day scrape the abscess internally, and then extract a larger portion, and repeat this several times according to its severity.
And especially if the patient is a young man, or a pregnant woman, or an infant, or an elderly person in poor health, for in such cases the vital spirit quickly resolves through the evacuation of the pus, and the patient easily recovers, and you should proceed with this treatment.
Therefore, guard this chapter with great caution, and when you make the incision in which you puncture these abscesses, clean the plaques and then consider whether the plaque of the abscess is small or a flat section; at that time, administer some of them or of oak bark. And if the abscess is large and the fissures of the incision are many, then it is necessary to place wool in each part until they heal.
And if in the abscess a part of the cord has been severed or you have concaved it around the circumference, then you should fill it with old wood shavings or threads made from linen cloth, as when you have treated bandages or dressings, without moisture; and strengthen that on the third day; and thereafter proceed to treat it and care for it with what is necessary of ointments until it is healed.
If blood flows during the time of your operation, then give water to wash and prepare some vinegar in which you dip a cloth, and place that over the spot where the blood is flowing for several times.
If the flow of blood continues, then you should administer treatment and care according to the powders which I have recommended in various places of this our book and division.
If it is in the time of winter, and the location of the abscess is on various nerves, then you should mix powders in vinegar and heated oil, and apply those to the affected areas.
And if it is in summer, and the areas are fleshy, then you should apply powders soaked in water and oil or in vinegar and oil, and do this washing every day for three days as we have said. Then you should lance the abscess, clean it, and administer whatever is appropriate for its treatment until it is healed.
And this is what is necessary for the knowledge of the treatment of abscesses universally, but according to the method of distinction I have already said about every abscess in which manner the cure of it should be carried out separately by chapters.
Chapter 41.
On the Section of Abscesses That Occur in the Neck of the Head.
In the neck of the head, small abscesses occur, and these are of various types of nodes that contain tunics within them; and the types of their contents vary.
And they are soft, and what they contain is a moisture similar to jelly. Of those among which I contain humidity similar to flour, and resembling them; and of those that are stony, hard.
And in the section of all, and in the extraction of those there is no fear, as the extraction of those does not contradict surgery.
And the operation in the section of those is that you express them with an instrument whose form approaches this, which is called an entremes, until you know what it contains.
For if what it contains is humidity, then you should divide that with a section according to its length by making a superficial section according to this form:
And begin the section from the line of .B. to the line of .G. Then, as the humidity is evacuated, you should excise that skin which contains the humidity, and do not leave any part of it behind, for if any part remains, it may cause trouble later.
And then immerse the piece in Egyptian ointment, if it is available, and if not, in water and salt; and apply this to the wound and leave it for another day, as this will dissolve everything that remains of that skin.
And then apply the Egyptian ointment to that piece again for a second and third time if necessary, until you are confident that there is no remaining part of that skin; now treat the wound with the ointment until it is healed.
And if an abscess contains hard nodules, then you should incise that according to this form: with a section having the shape of a cross, and insert hooks between both lips of the section and scrape it thoroughly from all sides, and exert your skill in extracting the membrane that contains it.
If there is opposition to what I have said about surgery, then at that time do what I have recounted first.
And similarly, treat the mature abscess with regard to its section and cure as we have told you; and the section of a mature abscess is easier, because it has little blood and little moisture.
And sometimes there are abscesses on the head in some people where there is not much moisture; the cause of this is that I incised an abscess on the head of an old woman and found it as hard as a stone, rough, white, which could not be crushed, and if anyone were to strike it, it would injure them.
However, in other abscesses on the head, this is not the case of this chapter; likewise, for abscesses that occur on children's heads and behind the ears, the section of all these should be a superficial incision.
And pause the puncture of those in the lower part so that the contents of the abscess can drain to the lower parts.
And treat those accordingly as is suitable for that cure.
Chapter XLII.
On the incision of scrofulas which occur in the neck.
These abscesses often occur in the neck and armpits, and sometimes they also appear in other parts of the body.
And those that occur in the neck often develop between them, and every scrofula among them is within its own proper layer, just as in knots and abscesses of the head, as we have recounted.
The species of these scrofulas are motes, for only some of them are lithic, and of those only some contain moisture, and of those only the malignant ones which do not obey cure.
Then in that one which you find to be well disposed by examination, of which the color of what is manifest is appropriate to the color of the gland, and it is swollen all over, and is not attached to the nerves of the neck, nor to the veins, nor to the artery, and is not pressed, so that you incise it at dry superficially from above the part below the body line G. between the line B., and peel it off entirely, and extend two lips of the gland an inch or inches if you need those, as we have said regarding the abscesses of the head, and extract that little by little.
And it is safer not to cut the vein or nerve.
And let the spatula not be sharp, so that it does not cause you to cut unnecessarily or disturb the patient, and do not incise what is not necessary to incise; for if you should cut a vein or artery and stop your operation, then pause with a vitriol paste or other powders which promote blood flow, and bandage the wound, and leave that inside where the acuteness of the abscess subsides and the swelling becomes mollified and begins to suppurate. When the blood is absorbed.
Then return to your operation once you have completed it.
And then inquire at the time of the operation if there is any cause for the other small scrofulas, so you can incise those and clean them.
And if there is a large vein in the region of the scrofula, avoid cutting into that area around the scrofula. And be careful to tie a very firm ligature above it and let the rest of it fall out by itself without harm.
And then fill the wound with old lint that you have already soaked in Egyptian pepper decoction, and then dress it.
And if you incise the entire scrofula, then make sure to approximate the two edges of the wound and sew them together immediately so that there is no room for any excess fluid.
But if you see that there is excess fluid due to the size of the scrofula, then it is necessary for you to incise its root, and drain it and administer sutures as mentioned.
And for the scrofulas that contain moisture, make a superficial puncture where it appears to you is the site of maturation, and pause before making further punctures deep into the base of the swelling as we have said.
And then administer punctures, cover them with appropriate applications and similar treatments, so that it corrodes what remains of the corruption. And when you see that the wound is already clean, then dress it with a healing flesh-generating poultice until it is healed.
Chapter XLIII.
On the incision of the pustule of an accidental swelling in the groin.
The ancients call this section in the epitome, and I have not seen any man in our land who has performed that incision.
And this is the inscription of the speech of those people.
In men who have a squint, it is advisable to avoid the extraction of the epilhot, as by doing this there would be no benefit since all the veins and the main ones of the malady are here.
In those who have boils in the mouth or throat or in both ears, when the illness is not in the bone, it is advisable to use the section of epilhot to avoid the loss which is caused by perforation.
Therefore, when we want to do this, we should incise the epilhot below three circles of its circles, or four for a smaller section along the latitude in that which is between two circles by quantity, so that the section is in ciphac, not in the cartilage, and this place is suitable for section because it is devoid of flesh and the vessels of blood there are few.
And if the surgeon is afraid, it is advisable to stretch out the throat skin by one inch, and then cut the skin until he reaches the canal, but avoid the vessels of blood if you see any reason for that.
And then incise the ciphac as we have recommended; and it is significant for the section of the canal by the flap which is from that tissue and by the separation of the voice.
And let the wound be left open for some time.
Thus, when the hour is chosen for which the puncture is feared, add two lips of the wound's edge, and cut through that single layer to the cartilage.
And then administer medicines that promote the growth of flesh until it is healed.
And Al-Bucasis says that the essence of what we have recounted is to see that some of these abscesses have already obstructed the patient's throat, and the patient has come close to death, and the air passage is cut off, and some would incise the epiglottis so that the patient can breathe over the site of the wound by some respiration, and thus be saved from death.
And by this commandment allow the wound to remain open until the malignity of the illness is consumed; and the malignity lasts for three days; therefore, at that hour command to treat the wound, and care for it until it is healed.
And what I have seen with my own eyes is that a servant took a knife and cut into her throat and severed part of the windpipe there. I was called to treat her, and I found the wound as if it were that of a dead person, and uncovered the wound and saw the blood that had come out of the wound in small amounts.
Thus, I confessed that she had not cut any vein or artery, and the air was coming out of the wound, and I treated her until she was fully healed.
And the servant did not suffer any harm except for hoarseness in her voice, and after some days she returned to improvement in her condition.
Here I say that in the section of the episiotomy there is no fear.
Chapter XLIV.
About the section on abscess which occurs in the groin area, and is called hernia of the groin.
This abscess called hernia of the groin is large according to the size of the body, and it occurs in women.
And it happens in two ways, either naturally or accidentally.
And in the natural case, there is no need for treatment.
And the accidental case happens in two ways, one of which is similar to fatty knots, and the other way is similar to an abscess caused by arterial obstruction, and in that case there is fear. And it is not appropriate to attempt treatment with iron except in the case where it is small. And you should be cautious about that and investigate it as described. If you find it similar to fatty knots and it is not attached to any veins, then incise it as you would with knots and extract it using water that contains substances from the peel and bursiclam; if not, thoroughly examine its nature, and subsequently treat the area with what is appropriate for internal treatment until it is healed.

Chapter XLVII.
On the treatment of men's breasts that are similar to those of women.
Some wounds cause the breasts of some men to swell as they begin to heal, and when the breasts are swollen, and when the breasts of women are assembled and rounded, leave them alone.

If the breast inclines to the sides and is soft due to its size, similar to how it might be in women, then cut it into two parts so that each pus can exit separately, in sections resembling a lunar shape, of which each should fit within the other except at their ends, such that the larger line contains the smaller one according to this form from the line .B. and the line .G. And then scrape off the edge between the two lips of the wound, remove the fat, and administer what we have mentioned about suturing and powders as necessary until it is healed.
And if you do not complete the incision of what needs to be cut due to the patient's restlessness and blood flow, then you should fill the wound with cloth submerged in a corrosive liquid and leave it until that corrodes what is hard in the fat, and then care for it until it is healed.

On the Piercing of Abscesses that Come from Below the Armpit.
Cut open abscesses that I see deeper with a lancet for the species of scrofula, hard ones, which have a cover that is thick.

Chapter XLIX.
On the incision of abscesses that occur due to arterial or venous causes.
When an artery is ruptured and the vein that is above it becomes consolidated, then abscesses may occur. The signs by which it can be known whether inflammation and abscess are due to an artery or a vein: for when an abscess is due to an artery, it tends to aggregate in the upper part of the body; and when you probe the abscess with your fingers, you feel a hissing sound.
And an abscess due to a vein is located closer to the surface of the body.
And to treat an abscess in these areas is a mistake, especially those on the armpits, and at the elbows, and on the neck, and in many places on the body; for it is serious, therefore care should be taken to avoid its treatment with iron, and those that are in the extremities or on the head should be avoided.
For one who is due to it from the inflammation of the artery opening, divide in the longitudinal section lengthwise; and then carefully make the incision with hooks and near the artery, and remove the tunics until it is exposed.
And then place on that needle and make it penetrate into the other side, and secure the artery with double thread in two places, — which I explain in detail in the extraction of two arteries which are in the thighs.
And then apply to the place which is between two ligaments with a spatula so that the blood stops there completely, and the abscess dissolves.
And then administer treatment in which pus is generated so that the ligaments fall off; and then treat it with appropriate ointments until it is healed.
And if the abscess is due to the section of a vein, now you should have in your hand what is possible regarding the abscess with the proper tools, and then insert the needle below the place where you had your hand, and make it penetrate; and tie this thread doubly so that you can extract it from the other side, and then ligature the abscess with a strong ligament as I have told you about the grapevine ligature on both sides of the thread's extremities.
If you fear that you will remove the thread, then now insert the needle with some wax below the abscess; should the point of the needle be first inserted, and strengthen the threads at four places.
When the abscess has become dry in its middle part so that what is inside it can come out, then you incise the excess of the skin, and leave what is attached to it.
And then apply to the wound the powder which you have mixed with vinegar and oil, and then administer the treatment made with cords and herbs until it is healed.
Chapter on the abscess that occurs due to the twisting of nerves.
Just as an abscess can occur in arteries and veins, and similarly, an abscess can occur in the nerves when they are struck or due to excessive labor, and by analogy.
And it is done with the thread in the areas of the assistants or the heel, or in any place where the joints are usually painful.
And it is a severe abscess, and its color resembles that of the body, and it is among the major conditions without fever, and when it is pressed with force, the patient seems to be in a stupor.
And it is not an abscess aggregated at the front of the body, and therefore it is below the skin, and it hurts all around and does not go to the parts in front or behind.
Therefore, when it is in the joints, there is no need for it to be treated with iron, as it will likely lead to contraction.
Make a cut in the head or forehead with a spatum (a type of surgical instrument). If it is a small abscess, incise it with forceps and then drain it by scraping.
And if it is large, then suspend drainage with an incision, and excise it; then apply a poultice. And close the wound with sutures, and treat it until it is healed.
Chapter 11.
On the incision of an abscess that occurs on the cheek as it occurs on the abdomen.
Therefore, for some people, there are visible swellings in their abdomens and other parts of their bodies, which are called funguses by similarity to mushrooms, whose cause is subtle but the appearance is large; and often the edges of these are smooth, and they can be small or greatly enlarged.
And I have seen one such case where in his abdomen there were two parts that resembled mushrooms, and there was no difference between those white ones, of fine texture.
And the edges of those were turned inward and would split open, and moisture would constantly run from them.
Therefore, I incised them and found within one about eighteen ounces and the other about ten ounces.
And the procedure in incising them is that you should consider whether the condition is humid, and if the color of the swelling is white, humid, with a fine texture; then you incise it with a broad spatum, and immediately in your presence cauterize it over fire, because in such cases the incision expels much blood; and if there is bleeding, cauterize that.
And if the wound is small and fearful, guard against cutting with iron; but now take fine lead recently made, and bind it to that part, the method of which we have described; and leave it there for two days.
And attach it to the constriction of the lead thread; therefore, do not stop binding more lead as needed until it is separated and falls off on its own.
But if the part to be cut is of thick tissue, now in cutting it there is some cause for fear and dread, especially when it is in the abdomen.
But it is possible that you can cut half of it, and then cauterize that so that it does not return.
And then treat it until the wound is healed.
And be careful that you do not presume to cut a part that is dark in color, has little sensation, and is easily movable, for such a part is often cancerous.
And this will come to mind as a reminder of that advice.
Chapter LII.
On the treatment of an umbilical hernia.
An umbilical hernia is caused by various reasons; it may be due to fissures in the abdominal wall above the abdomen, and for this, a patch or intestine segment is used depending on other ruptures; or it can be due to inflammation from a vein or artery that bleeds, or due to trapped air.
But if it is due to a fissure in the abdominal wall and the protrusion of a patch, now the color of the swelling is similar to the color of the body; it is painless, and then appears in various situations. And if it is due to the exit of the bowel, then at that moment the situation of that thing differs greatly from what we have recounted, and when you press that spot with your fingers, it is hidden, and immediately returns; and it is very light there, and it is magnified when you introduce bath water and vigorous labor.
And if it is due to moisture, then it is loose and not hidden when you press with your hand, nor is it constricted, nor is it hard.
And if it is due to blood, then at this sign the abscess appears as a declining black color.
And if it is due to flesh without moisture, then the abscess is severe, thick and hard, and it is embedded in proportion to a quantity.
And if it is due to gas, then the touch of it is soft.
And the operation in this case is that you consider now whether the prominence of the navel is due to blood from an artery, or a vein, or gas; now be cautious about treating it, for there is fear and dread as I have taught you in the chapter where I have discussed abscesses from arteries and veins.
And if the prominence of the navel is due to the bowel or the membrane, then you should order the patient to take their clothing off and stand extended; then examine around the entire navel with your hand, and then instruct them to lie on their back; then encircle with a splint around the circumference of the navel over the spot where you have marked with your hand; then extend half of the abscess above with about an inch; then tie it around the circumference tightly or loosely in a proper manner.
From the side of the abscess, lift up the membrane spread over the ligament and insert your finger into that pus to seek the sac; and if you have found or secured it by the ligament, then immediately extract it and push the sac to the inner parts of the abdomen.
And if you have found the membrane, then grasp it with a probe; and incise the excess tissue around it.
But if it is contrary to your artery or vein, then surround that spot, and return to your operation; and take two needles and place them in those two strong points and insert two needles around the circle you made around the abscess in a cross shape, which should penetrate; and then divide the abscess into four parts over the needles.
And if you wish, remove the needles and leave the area so that the extended flesh can drain and fall off on its own; or incise it when it has become thin and will drain, and then treat the membrane with a lotion appropriate for healing until it is healed.
And if the prominence of the navel is of flesh that has become hard or due to moisture, then you should treat the abscess as we have said and extract the blood or moisture that you find there, and then treat it with a lotion appropriate for healing and consolidating the area.
Chapter LIII.
On the Treatment of Wounds.
We have already said in the division about the types of wounds and in what manner they should be treated with medicines, and that it is necessary for the treatment to avoid instruments so that the wound does not become ulcerated; and we have described wounds generated in the first place and the caution in their treatment.
And the ancients say that in some cases it is necessary to remove [the tumor] in a place where its eradication is possible, just as they do with crabs that are in the breasts or armpits and similar parts of the body, especially when they start small.
But when it is old and hard, do not attempt to remove it yourself, for I cannot heal anyone from that nor have I seen another who could achieve this.
And the operation on it should be performed when it is appropriate, as we have said, by proceeding and leaving the patient to purge from black bile for some days, and then lance that [tumor] if there is a clearly evident swelling.
And then prepare the patient for the operation in which the procedure is to be performed, and afterward apply the hooked instruments that are needed for it; and then thoroughly clean all around with a good scalpel to ensure proper excision so that no cause remains for the recurrence of that [condition]. And let the blood flow freely, and do not apply bandages too tightly, and press the areas, and wipe away the thick blood with your hand or with an instrument that is suitable among those available to you.
But if it is contrary to have thick blood flowing and you need to stop the bleeding from a vein or artery, then cauterize that point until the flow of blood has stopped, and afterward treat that with another method until it is healed.
Chapter 46.
On the treatment of hydrops (edema or dropsy).
We have already recommended, in the division, the types of hydrops related to water, and the signs of each type, as well as the treatment of it with medicines.
In the case where iron is used for treatment, it applies only to the type of fracture known as "althitas," and not to approximating with iron in the types of fractures called "timpanistres" or "yposarcha," for that would be fatal.
And when you have already treated this type of hydrops called "timpanistres" with medicines and do not feel confident in your treatment, consider whether the patient has become weakened or suffers from another illness similar to this hydrops, as if they were suffering from coughs or conditions affecting the chest or belly and similar to those, then be careful not to treat them with iron, for there is danger in doing so.
But if you see the patient with abundant vigor and there is no other illness except this hydrops alone, and neither child nor elderly person, then the method of the operation for them is that you lift the patient between your arms, and the assistant presses the abdomen of the patient with their hand, expelling the water from below the ribcage, and then take a sharp spoon in this way:
it should be of two sharp points long, with a sharp tip like a spoon; however, there should be some gradual narrowing little by little, so that in the operation you do not penetrate into the bowel, and thereby harm the patient.
And then consider whether the origin of the hydrops is from the bowels, for if it is, you should distance yourself from the navel by three fingers' width at the lower parts, on the right side above the ribcage.
But if the origin of the hydrops is from a kidney illness, then your incision should be to the left of the navel by three fingers' width.
And if the generation of it is from the gallbladder, then let your incision be on the right side.
And it is not necessary for your incision to be on the side where the patient lies, so that the superfluities do not run to that place by reason of the pressure.
And then pierce completely with the instrument the gallbladder, and then insert into that incision, and raise your hand between the gallbladder and the sphincter, and you shall extract it; and if its quantity is one ounce or thereabouts.
And then pierce the sphincter so that the pus reaches the empty place, which is the site of the water. And then extract that and insert an instrument whose form is as follows: and it resembles a thin silver cannula; it is made of silver or ivory or lion's leather, at the lower part of which there is a small hole, and on its sides are three holes: two on one side and one on the other side; and the end of it is cut like the tip of a feather, as you see.
And at the upper end of it there is a ring, for when the instrument reaches the water, then immediately the patient should sit upon the instrument, thus evacuating an appropriate amount of water in that moment, for if you evacuate too much beyond what is necessary within an hour, the patient may die from resolution of their vital spirit, or it will hasten death which is near.
But evacuate that according to the quantity of the strength of the patient and according to how their condition, the strength of their pulse, and their overall health indicate to you.
Here is the translation:
Then leave the instrument in for another day if the patient tolerates it well, and extract a small amount of water from it, and use this water for several days out of fear, and guard yourself against error so that you do not remove too much water but only a little.
If you fear for the patient and release a large amount of water, now bury him in fine sand, pour sweat-inducing substances over him, and let him lie in the sun for a long time; and treat him with drying medicines until he is healed.

Chapter 55.
On the treatment of children who are born with unopened passages for urine.
Sometimes some of the children are born from their mother's womb with the head of their urethra not pierced (or it is blocked or not in its place).
Therefore, you should perform the piercing as soon as the child is born using a fine instrument according to this form:
And then insert a fine lead needle into the obstruction and leave it there for three days or four.
And when he needs to urinate, remove it and let him urinate; then return it afterward.
And if you do not insert the lead, it is possible that the urine which flows over that area will not remove this obstruction.
Let him whose wound is narrow be treated with a lead nail as we have said, for so many days until it is enlarged.
Let those in whom the wound is not in its proper place be treated as mentioned, the cause of which is that one who is born with the urethra below the tip of the penis cannot urinate normally because he must raise his penis upwards; and it is not for sexual activity, so the semen cannot reach the larger second passage correctly, and this is a serious condition.
And the method of the operation is that the patient lies on his back, and you grasp the tip of the penis with your left hand firmly, and incise the head of the penis in the location of the urethra with a sharp knife, like an incision for plucking feathers, or shave some part without cutting, so that the middle of the urethra resembles the tip of the penis and that the wound falls in its proper place as required.
And be careful during your operation to stop bleeding, as this often happens; and pause at the point where you need to stop the blood, and treat the wound until it is healed.
Chapter LVI.
Of the inflammation that occurs in the foreskin at the head of the penis, and of corruption, blackening, and adherence of the foreskin to the head of the penis.
This inflammation often occurs in the penis and is characterized by a prominent swelling of the flesh.
And one of these conditions is malignant and the other is non-malignant.
For benign cases, suspend one ounce of the subtle medicine and excise that which contains all the tumors; then apply to that part a poultice made with Egyptian onion; afterwards treat it with decoctions until it is healed.

But if the time is prolonged with this, there is an adjusted fissure in the rectum through which the bag descends into the rectum; and it happens that because of the extension of the rectum, which is near the hemorrhoids as we have said, the cause being that the rectum is stretched and thus becomes soft and swollen, and it needs to be examined.
And the treatment for this is with cautery as has been described in the preceding narrative.
And in some cases, it is treated with iron according to this method: the patient lies on their back between two chairs, and then the area of the rupture of the abscesses is dried by cutting across its width as needed.
And then stretch the white rectum below the cord until it is revealed.
And then take the cautery and place it on the prominent area of the rectum, and press it against the front of the abdomen.
And then sew the two prominent points on the edges of the rectum together with stitches.
From this extract the extremity of the vein should be tied off, and you should not incise the circumference completely, nor extend the opening, nor any other such cause as I will make you know in the treatment of an intestinal hernia.
And in the treatment of this condition with the treatment of wounds, when you incise the abscesses, clean that area and restore the wound until it is healed; for the circumference is contracted and the prominence of rupture is not adjusted.
And cautery is best in this place, for it is closer to health.
Chapter LXVIII.
On the softening of the cord of the testicles.
In many cases, the cord of the testicles is softened in some men because the flesh that lies within it is softened, and this requires careful attention.
Then it is necessary for the one who treats this condition to have the patient lie according to his side, and incise the entire cord that is softened over the natural cord; and then adjust two edges with suturing.
And if you wish, remove the excess of the softened cord at three or four places and with a firm suture.
And then incise between the sutures; and afterward treat as you would for other wounds until it is healed and the abscesses subside.
Chapter LXIX.
On Castration.
Know that castration in our law is forbidden, but it is read to me that I must remember it in this book; and the remembrance of it is not necessary except for two ways, one of which is so that when asked about it, the physician may know how to cure those who suffer from it; and the other way is that we have sometimes a need for castration in other animals for our use by them, such as horses, oxen, and pigs, and similar beasts.
And therefore I say that castration is performed in two ways: either by excision or by cutting and division.
But in the one that is performed by excision, the method of the operation is that we should bathe the animal in warm water until the testicles become soft and relaxed and hang down. And then take those [testicles] with your hand until they are softened and do not appear to be hurt by the touch.
But in castration performed by cutting and division, make sure you hold the animal and press the root of the testicles with your left hand.
And then grasp the spermatic cords, and make an incision on each side so that two halves are separated.
And then cut those parts after you have peeled each one away. And do not leave any cause for infection on those parts, but make the incision subtle so that it is above the veins.
And this method of castration, which is performed by excision, is better because it leaves no cause from the testicles for the animal to desire copulation.

Chapter LXX.
On the treatment of hermaphrodism.
Hermaphrodozia in men is recognized in two ways: the first occurs when there appears a space between the testicles where female characteristics are present, such as hair in that area.
And sometimes in those cases, urine is discharged from the area between the testicles.
In women, it is recognized in this way: the part of the woman above the pubis appears as if there are two testicles of a man slightly below and forward, like the scrotum of a man, containing two testicles.
The treatment is of three kinds: two for men and one for women. It is necessary that you incise the tightened flesh to allow the discharge of the harmful substance, and then treat it as you would other illnesses.
And in the second kind for men, where urine is discharged from the area between the testicles, there is no treatment or surgery for it.
Chapter XXI.
On cutting and raising flesh due to causes in women.
Cutting should be done lightly according to natural causes, ensuring it is done carefully and with proper regard; sometimes in women, it may need to be more extensive, like in men, so that it does not interfere during intercourse.
Then you should hold the excess flesh with your hand or with forceps and cut it.
In making an incision, especially at the root of the nail, so that there is no flow of blood.
And for the treatment of those wounds until they are healed.
Malignant flesh is the flesh that arises from the corruption within the mother before it fills out those parts outside according to the appearance of hair (and for this reason some first called this "tail disease"); therefore we should incise it just as we would incise a tendon, and treat it until it is healed.
Chapter LXXII.
On the Treatment of Ingrown Toenails.
Ingrown toenail is when the nail of the woman has not pierced through, or the passage is too small. And it is either natural or accidental.
It is accidental due to a disease that has preceded it, and that condition is caused either by flesh that is not properly fitted or by thin or thick skin.
And it occurs either at the root of the uterus, or on its sides, or in the upper part of it, or in the lower part, and it prohibits menstruation and conception and pregnancy, and rather lightly also menstrual periods.
And the diagnosis of that condition is made by palpation with a speculum, if the obstruction is apparent; but if it is not apparent, then seek it using your fingers or with a probe.
But if the obstruction is due to thin tissue and is located between the two lips, then you should cut it and disrupt that obstruction.
And you should apply plasters to both lips, and also place the fingers of both hands on them.
And the woman should lie on her back, with her thighs spread apart, and then stretch both lips forcefully until that subtle suture is broken and the obstruction is opened.
And then take wool and soak it in oil and apply that to the area, and keep a man there for three days so that the cut site does not become consolidated.
But if the suture is thick and dense, now it is necessary for you to cut that with a lancet or with a myrtle leaf.
But if the obstruction is due to flesh, now suspend that for one inch, and then incise it.
And with you are the medicines that stop blood flow without bleeding, such as hystaceae, dragon's blood, and oak galls, mixed with egg white.
And then administer a lead tube that is wide so that the wound does not consolidate too quickly.
And keep that for several days and administer dry lint.
And then treat it with the other method of consolidation until it is healed.
And sometimes accidents occur in the major formation of other tissues, and now it is necessary to incise according to this method. But if this is due to a chronic abscess, then with the chronic abscess that is in the main part, do not cause any opposition or hindrance with iron in any way.
Chapter LXXIII.
On the treatment of hemorrhoids and tumors that occur in the female genital area.
Hemorrhoids are an inflammation of the veins inside the anus, from which blood flows continuously; and when these hemorrhoids become old, they form thrombi.
And now I have described the types of these conditions and their symptoms, and I will also describe which of them can be treated and which cannot be treated.
Therefore, I say that hemorrhoids and thrombi that occur internally and do not appear to the senses should not be treated with instruments.
But those that occur at the opening of the anus and which can be felt by touch are those that can be treated.
And it is necessary that you place the woman in a comfortable position and then grasp those hemorrhoids with forceps or rough cloth, and cut them with scissors.
And then powder should be applied to stop the bleeding from one of the hemostatic powders that do not cause irritation, such as acacia and similar substances.
And then press the area with cold compresses for one hour, and afterwards apply it to cold water.
And if the bleeding persists, then have the patient sit in a decoction of sumac and lemon rinds and pomegranate peels and similar substances.
And then take flour of barley and apply it with honey and sour grape juice to make a plaster on the affected area.
And if the blood is clotting, that is good; and otherwise, bring together both wound edges, and on the nipples make incisions.
And then take lint and apply it with the juice of cilantro or the juice of coriander or the juice of hyssop mixed with wine to that area, and make it adhere to the place; and afterwards treat the place with ointments until it is healed.
And treat it until it is healed.
Chapter LXXIV.
On the piercing of the uterus in accidental injury to the abdomen.
Various types of abscesses occur in the abdomen, such as boil, stone abscess, ulcerous abscess, matted abscess, scrotal abscess, hemorrhoids, and fistulas, and other abscesses. And I have already mentioned these illnesses and the types of them and the signs of them, and their treatments in detail.

During the operation, place the woman on a chair that has two arms; and recline her on her side and arrange her legs at the part below the stomach, and spread out her thighs, and let her hands rest above her knees, and bind some of it with bandages as is appropriate.

Chapter LXXV.

Chapter LXXVI.
On the Extraction of a Dead Fetus.
When you are treating a dead fetus as we have said in the division of medication and it does not come out by itself, and you must then use an operation, at this time it is necessary to consider whether the woman is of sound constitution and is not subject to any of those accidents for which her loss is feared.
At this time the woman should be placed on her back on the bed with her buttocks raised and her head lowered.
And the minister should hold her by both hands or tie her to the bed so that her body does not extend during the extraction of the fetus.
And then you should moisten the mouth of the mother with oils and honey, and with mucus made from henna, fenugreek, and linseed.
And then the midwife should anoint her hand with those oils and mucus, and then insert it gently into the mother, and then search with her hand for the place where the hooks are in the fetus.
And these are the appropriate places: then you should consider whether the fetus is positioned so that it will descend with its head down, and at this time you place the hooks in its hands, or in its neck, or in its mouth, or on its palate, or under its chin, or in its clavicle, or in the proper parts of its sides, or under its armpits.
But if the descent is with its feet down, then in the navel or in the middle of its back.
Take the needle with the right hand and place its curve at that point which is between the fingers of the left hand, and insert it easily into one of those places we have mentioned until it reaches the diseased area.
And place and fix it in such a position that another needle, or a third if necessary, can be inserted equally without stretching the straightness of the tissue.
And let it be fixed in all parts so that the extraction of it may be eased as is done with the removal of teeth.
And it is necessary in that place where the stretching should be softened; and if any part of it is retained, then it is necessary for the midwife to anoint some of those places with oil and insert them carefully and rotate what is retained.
Therefore, if a part of the fetus is delivered, then the needles should be moved to a place that is further along; and do this until all of the fetus is delivered.
But if the hand comes out before the other and it is not possible to reduce it due to the contraction of the tissue, then wrap a cloth around that one; and afterwards extract it until all of it is delivered, and cut it off either at the joint of the hand or at the elbow.
And do the same for the other hand and both feet.
But if the head of the fetus is large, or if there is contraction during delivery, or if it is in the tight water bag, then insert between the fingers and cut open the head to extract the water, or use an instrument called "alundat," the form of which will be among the shapes of other instruments in the chapter that follows this one.
And it should be done as if it were a large root by nature: and now it is necessary either to cut that which is bound up or to take away that which has grown, as we have said; and then extract them from the bones with the forceps.
And if the root is twisted and compressed by the furcula, then it should be split so that the moisture which is in the tissues may be released.
But if it is not complicated and does not twist, then you should cut the root as soon as possible according to what seems best to you.
And if the lower part of the abdomen is abscessed or is in a state of edema, then it is necessary for you to puncture that which contains the moisture that is there.
But if the growth is on the upper teeth, then the attraction of it is slight and the direction of it towards the mouth of the mother is also slight.
But if it is compressed by the abdomen and the tissues, then it is necessary for you to extract that which you have wrapped in a cloth with your hand, and to cut open the abdomen and the tissues so that the fluid that is there may run out.
But if the other parts remain still and only the root returns, then place your left hand between them; but if the mouth of the mother is open, then insert your hand into the pelvis, and search for the root, and pull it along with the others into the mouth of the mother, and then insert one or two fingers, and pull it along with those.
And if the mouth of the mother is compressed by an abscess that occurs on it, then it should not be troubled further; instead, it is necessary to administer moist and fatty applications. Administer plasters; and follow with waters that soften and moisten.
And if the condition is on their side, then immediately if possible puncture it; and administer the liquid that we have mentioned in the case of a live abscess.
And if that is not possible, then cut it into pieces and extract it.
And make sure that you do not leave any cause for a second occurrence.
And when you have completed your entire operation, then administer what we have mentioned for the treatment of abscesses that are similar to those just discussed.
And if there is bleeding, then apply styptic waters and administer the other treatment.
And I have seen a woman in whose abdomen there was a dead fetus, and above that focus another pregnancy occurred, and above the other focus the fetus was also dead. It happened to someone who had an abscess near their navel for a long time; it became internally filled with pus, and began to discharge pus.
And I was called to treat them, and treated them for a long time, but the condition did not heal.
Then I applied to them several causes of strong attraction in the form of plasters, and extracted one bone from them, and after a few days extracted another bone; and I was very surprised, as there were no bones in the abdomen.
And then I thought that they were bones from the dead fetus.
Therefore, when treating the wound, remove the bones that are present in its depths and which have already been exposed for some time, and correct it with a little force.
And do not be surprised if it seems strange, for in this lies the science and assistance to what the surgeon uses his hand to administer in treatment.
Of the forms of the instruments that are necessary for extracting the fetus.
Form of a spiral in which the main one is used:
This is the form of a stretcher on which the leaves are equalized, to this equalization there are two spirals at the two extremities of two rods. However, this spiral should be finer than the others, and it should be made of wire or the wood of trees.
And the width of each rod should be two fingers, and the margin on each side should be one finger, and the length of each is half a palm plus a bit more; and in the middle of the two rods there are two adjustments made of that same wood which are already fixed, whose length is half a palm plus a little more, and the width of each is two fingers or a little more.
And these two adjustments should be inserted into the mouth of the main one so that it can be opened by them when you revolve the two prescribed spirals.
Another similar form that is finer and lighter:

Of the extraction of the second [incisor].
When the second [tooth] is retained during childbirth, you should command the woman to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze under certain conditions. Place your hand over her mouth and nose, and if it comes out this way, it is good.
